Introduction   │    3  
© Menachem Education Foundation, 2016 . All rights reserved.  
I ntroduc tion  
1.  What is an interim assessment?  
Interim assessments are one of the critical steps in standards based learning and the Data 
Driven Instruction (DDI) cycle of curriculum mapping, assessment, analysis and action. An 
interim assessment is a form of assessment that educators use to evaluate where students 
are in their learning progress and determine whether they are on track with learning  goals.  
It is recommended that assessments be administered 3 to 5 times throughout the school 
year. In education, the term assessment refers to the wide variety of methods that 
educators use to evaluate, measure, and document the academic readiness, learn ing 
progress, and skill acquisition of students. The results derived from these assessments act 
as a valuable source of actionable data concerning students’ mastery of standards.  
2.  Why are these sample  assessment questions?  
Theoretically, you could be receiving 3 - 5 standardized assessments during the year from a 
centralized office, such as MEF, to administer to your students. However, we have 
specifically chosen not to provide universal interim assessments, for the following reasons.  
The foundation of s tandards based learning is that you, the teacher, drive the learning 
process by teaching for mastery .  Material can be taught, assessments given and graded, and 
yet not much achieved –  unless the teacher adopts the goal of helping every of one of his or 
her  students attain mastery of each of the standards.  
How does a teacher know how to plan instruction in order to facilitate mastery? How does a 
teacher know when and how to re - teach or review a particular standard? How can the 
teacher develop a deep enough u nderstanding of the learning standards to adequately 
convey them to his or her students?  
Individualized interim assessments answer all of these questions.  
Unlike the prevailing misconception, assessments are the starting point for instruction , not 
the endi ng point. This is why it is critical that you, the teacher, own the assessment process 
by taking responsibility for building each interim assessment.  
1.  By creating interim assessments, you are brought face to face with the standards, and 
gain a thorough und erstanding of each standard that you plan to teach.

## Page 4

ד”בס  
4    │    Introduction    
© Menachem Education Foundation, 2016 . All rights reserved.  
2.  By creating interim assessments before you begin teaching, you will have a much 
clearer idea of the goals of your teaching, having articulated what your students 
should know and be able to do with every s tandard once you have taught it to them.  
3.  The data on student mastery yielded from each interim assessment will help you 
create more rigorous and effective interim assessments as the year progresses.  
The sample assessment questions provided in this document  are meant to help you with 
this process, demonstrating the level of rigor that we intended for these standards at each 
grade level. They are intended as a reference to guide your efforts in creating interim 
assessments that will best suit your students’ i ndividual needs for standards mastery.  
3.  How to use this resource:  
For every standard we have provided a number of sample assessment questions. Though 
the questions are not delineated per grade, they are listed in order of increasing difficulty, 
so that the  first questions for each standard will be appropriate for the younger grades, and 
the later questions will be appropriate for older grades. Refer to the scope and sequence of 
each standard to identify the level of rigor that you are aiming for and select the questions 
from the range provided that best match your students’ level. (Of course, every grade 
should be assessed using questions with varying levels of difficulty, in order to pinpoint 
what level of mastery has been reached.)  
These questions are prov ided as suggestions . They are there to help you identify what your 
students should know and be able to do for each standard.  However, do not feel limited by 
these questions. Use these ideas or come up with your own as you build an assessment 
suited to your  class, as long as it is rigorous and authentic –  i.e., aligned to the standards.  
You will need to adapt many of the questions provided herein to the syllabus that you are 
working with. For standards that are text or content specific, you will need to ada pt these 
questions to פסוקים that your students have already encountered. For standards that 
require students to apply a particular skill to unlearned material (generally in grades 5 and 
6), you will need to select unlearned פסוקים or מפרשים to build your questions. Typically, 
for “learned פסוקים we used texts from ספר בראשית and for “unlearned פסוקים or 
רש"י s)” we used texts from ספר שמות but you will need to adapt according to what is 
familiar and unfamiliar to your students.

## Page 5

בס"ד  
Introduction   │    5  
© Menachem Education Foundation, 2016 . All rights reserved.  
4.  Appendices  
We included a number of resources as appendices to these sample assessments. These 
include:  
1.  Rubrics:  Rubrics are generally necessary for essay or extended response questions. 
Again, you can customize these rubrics according to your class or needs. Whatever 
your rubri c specifications may be, make sure that your class has a clear idea of what 
you are looking for before they are given the particular assignment.  
2.  Assessment Guidelines:  We include a summary of various kinds of assessments and 
guidelines for using them effe ctively, summarized from the book Classroom 
Assessment for Student Learning by Stiggins, Arter, Chappuis and Chappuis. This 
summary was prepared by Liz Gewirtzman, a master “teacher of teachers” and 
member of the MEF team of consultants. When it is not obv ious from the question 
itself, we let you know which category of assessment a particular question belongs to 
–  whether essay, fill in, or performance assessment. You can refer to these guidelines 
to find out more about each of the forms of assessment.  
5.   Our  Team  
The Zekelman Standards for חומש were developed by a team of educators under the 
auspices of the Menachem Education Foundation. The team is directed by Rabbi Yossi 
Rosenblum, principal of Yeshiva Schools, Pittsburgh, PA, and includes Rabbi Mendy 
Green baum, principal of Cheder Menachem, Los Angeles, CA; Mrs. Sara Rosenfeld, 
curriculum director at Beth Rivka/Yeshiva Colleges of Melbourne, AU; Rabbi Meir Perelstein, 
curriculum director at Darchei Menachem, Brooklyn, NY; and Mrs. Chanah Rose, former 
curric ulum director at the Shluchim Online School. All of these contributors, as well as the 
real time feedback from the schools they represent, helped to determine and refine the 
level of rigor intended by each standard. The assessment questions themselves were  
created by Rabbi Yossi Rosenblum and Mrs. Chanah Rose, incorporating questions by Rabbi 
Mendy Greenbaum and Mrs. Leah Hoffman as well.  
We would like to thank Mrs. Rena Udkoff for her expert editing of this document, and Rabbi 
Meir Perelstein for his layou t and design. We would also like to thank the entire team at 
MEF, most notably Rabbi Zalman Shneur, executive director, and Rabbi Shmuly  Goldman, 
vice president  and COO, for driving this process. Special appreciation is due to Mr. Alan 
Zekelman, a visionar y philanthropist, for making the Zekelman Standards Project possible.  
We wish you, the teacher, much success in the implementation of these assessments and 
Hatzlacha in this most sacred task entrusted upon you, educating the next generation of 
תורה true Je ws.  
The Zekelman Standards Development Team

1.1  ה”חכמתו ורצונו של הקב  
Note:  This standard c an be assessed in combination with other standards through essay questions and performance assessments. In 
particular, it can be incorporated into assessments for Standard 4, especially 4.9.  
 
 Face to face assessment:  Teacher observes student’s conduct and marks it against the checklist below.  
 Self - assessment :  student marks his or her own conduct against the checklist below.   
Grade 1  Grade 2  Grade 3  Grade 4  Grade 5  Grade 6  Grade 7  Grade 8  
1.1   ה"חכמתו ורצונו של הקב  
A. Relates to a ספר of  חומש with respect and affection as prescribed by הלכה and מנהג such as kissing the חומש after use and 
not putting it on the floor.  
B. Relates to study of חומש with appropriate reverence, as reflected in conduct according to הלכה and דרך ארץ such as washing 
נעגל וואסער and saying ברכות התורה before learning, and sitting respectfully).

© Menachem Education Foundation, 2016 . All rights reserved.  
This checklist can be adjusted for age appropriateness or grade level.  The t eacher can add items to the criteria  based on הלכות  
and behaviors that were taught.  
Criteria  Yes/No/Sometimes  Comments  
Treats the ספר with respect when storing it, by placing it 
on top of other ספרים or books, and not on a floor or 
seat.  
  
Treats the ספר with respect when learning from it, by not 
placing things on top of it, using it for other purposes, or 
leaving it open when taking a break.  
  
Treats the ספר with respect and affection upon finishing 
to learn, by closing it and kissing it.  
  
Washed וואסער נעגל in the morning.    
Said ברכת התורה in the morning.    
Washed נעגל וואסער again before learning if necessary.

 Yossi is carrying a heavy חוּמָשׁ and he feels very tired. Where is the most respectful place for him to put the חוּמָשׁ down?  
 On an empty floor, in the corner of the room.  
 On a table, as long as it is not under anything else.  
 On a couch that only one person is sitting on.  
 Ella is so excited to review חוּמָשׁ She tells her mother that she will even take the חוּמָשׁ and review it while she is lying down 
under her covers, about to go to sleep. What is the mother most likely to tell her?  
 It is always good to review חוּמָשׁ  . 
 חוּמָשׁ is supposed to be reviewed while sitting respectfully.  
 חוּמָשׁ is supposed to be reviewed only in school.  
 Yon i tells his older sister Tirzah that he wants to do something special for his birthday: as soon as he wakes up and washes 
negel vasser, he will learn some תּוֹרָה even before he gets out of bed. What is Tirzah most likely to say?  
 It is respectful to learn  תּוֹרָה before you even get out of bed.  
 It is respectful to learn תּוֹרָה before you eat breakfast.  
 It is not respectful to learn תּוֹרָה before you say בִּרְכַת הַתּוֹרָה  . 
 It is not respectful to learn תּוֹרָה before you finish davening.

 Leave the חומש open on his desk.  
 Put his notebook  in side  the חומש before closing it to save the place.

 When I am learning חוּמָשׁ in America, it is the same חוּמָשׁ that is being learned in a different country.

1.1  ה"חכמתו ורצונו של הקב  
F. Knows that there is an orderly sequence to 
חומש that is usually chronological.  
F. Knows that there are sometimes deviations in the order of the חומש to 
bring out other messages than chronology, and quotes the מחז"ל   
"אין מוקדם ומאוחר בתורה"  . 
 True or False:  The main purpose of the תורה is to teach us our history.  
 Which sentence is true?  
 The תורה always goes in order, since its  main purpose is to teach us history .  
 The תורה sometimes does not go in order ,  since its main purpose is not to teach us history.  
 The תורה never goes in order, and we cannot learn our history from the תורה  . 
 Why does the תורה sometimes relate stories out of  chronological order?  
 Because chronological order is never important.  
 To teach us something in addition to the storyline.  
 Because there are differences in opinion about the correct order.  
 Why are events in the תורה sometimes not written in chronological order?  
 Chronological order doesn’t matter because תורה is not a history book.  
 Because the תורה wants to teach us something by placing this particular story/event out of order.  
 Because the תורה tells stories in order of their importance.  
 Because there are different opinions about the chronological order.

 Which ל”מאמר חז tells us that the תורה does not always go in order since its main purpose is not to be a history book?

 ה”חכמתו ורצונו של הקב  
 ן מוקדם ומאוחר בתורהאי  
 Fill in the blanks: ___________ _____________ אין מוקדם

Note:  This standard can be assessed in combination with other standards through essay questions and performance assessments.  In

1.2  תורה מלשון הוראה  
A. Recognizes that there is a 
lesson to be learned from 
every topic in חומש  . 
A. When a lesson has been learned, thinks of ways that the lesson applies in their personal life.  
 B. Understands that the word 
תורה is related to הוראה  , 
indicating that the primary 
purpose of תורה is to teach us 
lessons for our lives.  
B. Students expect personal relevance and lessons in עבודת ה  
in every topic in חומש  .

6And Abraham  took the wood for the burnt offering, and he placed [it] upon his son 
Isaac, and he took into his hand the fire and the knife, and they both went together.  
 ווַיִּקַּח אַבְרָהָם אֶת עֲצֵי הָעֹלָה וַיָּשֶׂם עַל יִצְחָק בְּנוֹ וַיִּקַּח בְּיָדוֹ 
וְאֶת הַמַּאֲכֶלֶת וַיֵּלְכוּ שְׁנֵיהֶם יַחְדָּו: אֶת הָאֵשׁ  
7And Isaac spoke to Abraham his father, and he said, "My father!" And he said, "Here I 
am, my son." And he said, "Here are the fire and the wood, but where is the lamb for 
the burnt offering?"  
 יִצְחָק אֶל אַבְרָהָם אָבִיו וַיֹּאמֶר אָבִי וַיֹּאמֶר הִנֶּנִּי בְנִי זוַיֹּאמֶר 
וַיֹּאמֶר הִנֵּה הָאֵשׁ וְהָעֵצִים וְאַיֵּה הַשֶּׂה לְעֹלָה:  
8And Abraham said, "God will provide for Himself the lamb for the burnt offering, my 
son." And they both went together.  
 חוַיֹּאמֶר אַבְרָהָם אֱלֹהִים יִרְאֶה לּוֹ הַשֶּׂה לְעֹלָה בְּנִי וַיֵּלְכוּ 
שְׁנֵיהֶם יַחְדָּו:  
9And they came to the place of which God had spoken to him, and Abraham built the 
altar there and arranged the wood, and he bound Isaac his son and placed him  on the 
altar upon the wood.  
 טוַיָּבֹאוּ אֶל הַמָּקוֹם אֲשֶׁר אָמַר לוֹ הָאֱלֹהִים וַיִּבֶן שָׁם אַבְרָהָם 
אֶת הַמִּזְבֵּחַ וַיַּעֲרֹךְ אֶת הָעֵצִים וַיַּעֲקֹד אֶת יִצְחָק בְּנוֹ וַיָּשֶׂם 
אֹתוֹ עַל הַמִּזְבֵּחַ מִמַּעַל לָעֵצִים:  
10And Abraham stretched  forth his hand and took the knife, to slaughter his son.   יוַיִּשְׁלַח אַבְרָהָם אֶת יָדוֹ וַיִּקַּח אֶת הַמַּאֲכֶלֶת לִשְׁחֹט אֶת בְּנוֹ  
11And an angel of God called to him from heaven and said, "Abraham! Abraham!" 
And he said, "Here I am."  
 א אֵלָיו מַלְאַךְ יְהֹוָה מִן הַשָּׁמַיִם וַיֹּאמֶר אַבְרָהָם יאוַיִּקְרָ 
אַבְרָהָם וַיֹּאמֶר הִנֵּנִי:  
12And he said, "Do not stretch forth your hand to the lad, nor do the slightest thing to 
him, for now I know that you are a God fearing man, and you did not withhold your 
son, your only one, from Me."  
 יבוַיֹּאמֶר אַל תִּשְׁלַח יָדְךָ אֶל הַנַּעַר וְאַל תַּעַשׂ לוֹ מְאוּמָה כִּי 
עַתָּה יָדַעְתִּי כִּי יְרֵא אֱלֹהִים אַתָּה וְלֹא חָשַׂכְתָּ אֶת בִּנְךָ אֶת 
יְחִידְךָ מִמֶּנִּי:

ידוע שעשו וישקהו: נקוד עליו, ויש חולקין בדבר הזה .... יש שדרשו נקודה זו לומר שלא נשקו בכל לבו. אמר ר' שמעון בן יוחאי הלכה היא ב

There are dots over the word. There is controversy concerning this matter …. Some interpret the dots to mean that he did not 
kiss him wholeheartedly. Rabbi Shimon ben Yochai said: It is a well  known tradition that Esav hated Yaakov, but his compassion 
was moved at that time, and he kissed him wholeheartedly .

 In a chumash, we find many symbols called the “ta’amei hamikra” which can help  the ba’al koreh know how to properly 
“sing” the  Torah reading in shul.   They can also be helpful to you in learning Chumash, even if you are not singing it. How?  
 They can tell you which words in the פסוק are a quotation (showing that someone is speaking).  
 They can tell you which words in the פסוק are most important.  
 They can tell you which words in the פסוק should be read together and when you should pause.  
 They can tell you which words in the פסוק are a question.

 From the נקודות  .

 From the כתב  .

 Punctuation marks  
 Correct spelling  
 Rules of grammar

## Page 69

בס"ד  
Introduction   │    3  
© Menachem Education Foundation, 2016 . All rights reserved.  
I ntroduction  
1.  What is an interim assessment?  
Interim assessments are one of the critical steps in standards based learning and the Data 
Driven Instruction (DDI) cycle of curriculum mapping, assessment, analysis and action. An 
interim assessment is a form of assessment that educators use to evaluate where students 
are in their learning progress and determine whether they are on track with learning goals.  
It is recommended that assessments be administered 3 to 5 times throughout the sch ool 
year. In education, the term assessment refers to the wide variety of methods that 
educators use to evaluate, measure, and document the academic readiness, learning 
progress, and skill acquisition of students. The results derived from these assessments  act 
as a valuable source of actionable data concerning students’ mastery of standards.  
2.  Why are these sample  assessment questions?  
Theoretically, you could be receiving 3 - 5 standardized assessments during the year from a 
centralized office, such as MEF, to  administer to your students. However, we have 
specifically chosen not to provide universal interim assessments, for the following reasons.  
The foundation of standards based learning is that you, the teacher, drive the learning 
process by teaching for mast ery .  Material can be taught, assessments given and graded, and 
yet not much achieved –  unless the teacher adopts the goal of helping every of one of his or 
her students attain mastery of each of the standards.  
How does a teacher know how to plan instructio n in order to facilitate mastery? How does a 
teacher know when and how to re - teach or review a particular standard? How can the 
teacher develop a deep enough understanding of the learning standards to adequately 
convey them to his or her students?  
Individu alized interim assessments answer all of these questions.  
Unlike the prevailing misconception, assessments are the starting point for instruction , not 
the ending point. This is why it is critical that you, the teacher, own the assessment process 
by taking responsibility for building each interim assessment.  
1.  By creating interim assessments, you are brought face to face with the standards, and 
gain a thorough understanding of each standard that you plan to teach.

## Page 70

בס"ד  
4    │    Introduction    
©  Menachem Education Foundation, 2016 . All rights reserved.  
2.  By creating interim assessments before you be gin teaching, you will have a much 
clearer idea of the goals of your teaching, having articulated what your students 
should know and be able to do with every standard once you have taught it to them.  
3.  The data on student mastery yielded from each interim as sessment will help you 
create more rigorous and effective interim assessments as the year progresses.  
The sample assessment questions provided in this document are meant to help you with 
this process, demonstrating the level of rigor that we intended for t hese standards at each 
grade level. They are intended as a reference to guide your efforts in creating interim 
assessments that will best suit your students’ individual needs for standards mastery.  
3.  How to use this resource :  
For every standard we have prov ided  a number of  sample assessment questions. Though 
the questions are not delineated per grade, they are listed in order of increasing difficulty, 
so that the first questions for each standard will be appropriate for the younger grades, and 
the later ques tions will be appropriate for older grades. Refer to the scope and sequence of 
each standard to identify the level of rigor that you are aiming for and select the questions 
from the range provided that best match your students’ level. (Of course, every gra de 
should be assessed using questions with varying levels of difficulty, in order to pinpoint 
what level of mastery has been reached.)  
These questions are provided as suggestions . They are there to help you identify what your 
students should know and be ab le to do for each standard.  However, do not feel limited by 
these questions. Use these ideas or come up with your own as you build an assessment 
suited to your class, as long as it is rigorous and authentic –  i.e., aligned to the standards.  
You will need to adapt many of the questions provided herein to the syllabus that you are 
working with. For standards that are text or content specific, you will need to adapt these 
questions to פסוקים that your students have already encountered. For standards that 
requ ire students to apply a particular skill to unlearned material (generally in grades 5 and 
6), you will need to select unlearned פסוקים or מפרשים to build your questions. Typically, 
for “learned פסוקים we used texts from ספר בראשית and for “unlearned יםפסוק or 
רש"י s)” we used texts from ספר שמות but you will need to adapt according to what is 
familiar and unfamiliar to your students.

## Page 71

בס"ד  
Introduction   │    5  
© Menachem Education Foundation, 2016 . All rights reserved.  
4.  Appendices  
We included a number of resources as appendices to these sample assessments. These 
include:  
1.  Rubrics:  Rubrics  are generally necessary for essay or extended response questions. 
Again, you can customize these rubrics according to your class or needs. Whatever 
your rubric specifications may be, make sure that your class has a clear idea of what 
you are looking for b efore they are given the particular assignment.  
2.  Assessment Guidelines:  We include a summary of various kinds of assessments and 
guidelines for using them effectively, summarized from the book Classroom 
Assessment for Student Learning by Stiggins, Arter, C happuis and Chappuis. This 
summary was prepared by Liz Gewirtzman, a master “teacher of teachers” and 
member of the MEF team of consultants. When it is not obvious from the question 
itself, we let you know which category of assessment a particular question  belongs to 
–  whether essay, fill in, or performance assessment. You can refer to these guidelines 
to find out more about each of the forms of assessment.  
5.   Our Team  
The Zekelman Standards for Chumash were developed by a team of educators under the 
auspices  of the Menachem Education Foundation. The team is directed by Rabbi Yossi 
Rosenblum, principal of Yeshiva Schools, Pittsburgh, PA, and includes Rabbi Mendy 
Greenbaum, principal of Cheder Menachem, Los Angeles, CA ; Mrs. Sara Rosenfeld, 
curriculum director at Beth Rivka/Yeshiva Colleges of Melbourne, AU ; Rabbi Meir Perelstein, 
curriculum director at Darchei Menachem, Brooklyn, NY ; and Mrs. Chanah Rose, former 
curriculum director at the Shluchim Online School. All of these contributors, as well as the 
real ti me feedback from the schools they represent, helped to determine and refine the 
level of rigor intended by each standard. The assessment questions themselves were 
created by Rabbi Yossi Rosenblum and Mrs. Chanah Rose, incorporating questions by Rabbi 
Mendy  Greenbaum and Mrs. Leah Hoffman as well.  
We would like to thank Mrs. Rena Udkoff for her expert editing of this document, and Rabbi 
Meir Perelstein for his layout and design. We would also like to thank the entire team at 
MEF, most notably Rabbi Zalman Sh neur, executive director, and Rabbi Shmuly  Goldman, 
vice president  and COO, for driving this process. Special appreciation is due to Mr. Alan 
Zekelman, a visionary philanthropist, for making the Zekelman Standards Project possible.  
We wish you, the teacher , much success in the implementation of these assessments and 
Hatzlacha in this most sacred task entrusted upon you, educating the next generation of 
Torah - true Jews.  
The Zekelman Standards Development Team

week. In general, ________ test is only hard if one has not studied.” “_________’s true,” said Moishy, resolving to always 
do his homewor k from then on.

## Page 134

בס"ד  
Introduction   │    3  
© Menachem Education Foundation, 2016 . All rights reserved.  
I ntroduction  
1.  What is an interim assessment?  
Interim assessments are one of the critical steps in standards based learning and the Data 
Driven Instruction (DDI) cycle of curriculum mapping, assessment, analysis and action. An 
interim assessment is a form of assessment that educators use to evaluate where students 
are in their learning progress and determine whether they are on track w ith learning goals.  
It is recommended that assessments be administered 3 to 5 times throughout the school 
year. In education, the term assessment refers to the wide variety of methods that 
educators use to evaluate, measure, and document the academic read iness, learning 
progress, and skill acquisition of students. The results derived from these assessments act 
as a valuable source of actionable data concerning students’ mastery of standards.  
2.  Why are these sample  assessment questions?  
Theoretically, you cou ld be receiving 3 - 5 standardized assessments during the year from a 
centralized office, such as MEF, to administer to your students. However, we have 
specifically chosen not to provide universal interim assessments, for the following reasons.  
The foundatio n of standards based learning is that you, the teacher, drive the learning 
process by teaching for mastery .  Material can be taught, assessments given and graded, and 
yet not much achieved –  unless the teacher adopts the goal of helping every of one of his or 
her students attain mastery of each of the standards.  
How does a teacher know how to plan instruction in  order to facilitate mastery? How does a 
teacher know when and how to re - teach or review a particular standard? How can the 
teacher develop a deep enough understanding of the learning standards to adequately 
convey them to his or her students?  
Individualiz ed interim assessments answer all of these questions.  
Unlike the prevailing misconception, assessments are the starting point for instruction , not 
the ending point. This is why it is critical that you, the teacher, own the assessment process 
by taking resp onsibility for building each interim assessment.  
1.  By creating interim assessments, you are brought face to face with the standards, and 
gain a thorough understanding of each standard that you plan to teach.

## Page 135

בס"ד  
4    │    Introduction    
© Menachem Education Foundation, 2016 . All rights reserved.  
2.  By creating interim assessments before you begin teaching, you will have a much 
clearer idea of the goals of your teaching, having articulated what your students 
should know and be able to do with every standard once you have taught it to them.  
3.  The data on student mastery yielded from each interim assess ment will help you 
create more rigorous and effective interim assessments as the year progresses.  
The sample assessment questions provided in this document are meant to help you with 
this process, demonstrating the level of rigor that we intended for these  standards at each 
grade level. They are intended as a reference to guide your efforts in creating interim 
assessments that will best suit your students’ individual needs for standards mastery.  
3.  How to use this resource :  
For every standard we have provided  a number of  sample assessment questions. Though 
the questions are not delineated per grade, they are listed in order of increasing difficulty, 
so that the first questions for each standard will be appropriate for the younger grades, and 
the later question s will be appropriate for older grades. Refer to the scope and sequence of 
each standard to identify the level of rigor that you are aiming for and select the questions 
from the range provided that best match your students’ level. (Of course, every grade 
s hould be assessed using questions with varying levels of difficulty, in order to pinpoint 
what level of mastery has been reached.)  
These questions are provided as suggestions . They are there to help you identify what your 
students should know and be able t o do for each standard.  However, do not feel limited by 
these questions. Use these ideas or come up with your own as you build an assessment 
suited to your class, as long as it is rigorous and authentic –  i.e., aligned to the standards.  
You will need to a dapt many of the questions provided herein to the syllabus that you are 
working with. For standards that are text or content specific, you will need to adapt these 
questions to פסוקים that your students have already encountered. For standards that 
require students to apply a particular skill to unlearned material (generally in grades 5 and 
6), you will need to select unlearned פסוקים or מפרשים to build your questions. Typically, 
for “learned פסוקים we used texts from ספר בראשית and for “unlearned פסוקים or 
רש"י s)” we used texts from ספר שמות but you will need to adapt according to what is 
familiar and unfamiliar to your students.

## Page 136

בס"ד  
Introduction   │    5  
© Menachem Education Foundation, 2016 . All rights reserved.  
4.  Appendices  
We included a number of resources as appendices to these sample assessments. These 
include:  
1.  Rubrics:  Rubrics are  generally necessary for essay or extended response questions. 
Again, you can customize these rubrics according to your class or needs. Whatever 
your rubric specifications may be, make sure that your class has a clear idea of what 
you are looking for befor e they are given the particular assignment.  
2.  Assessment Guidelines:  We include a summary of various kinds of assessments and 
guidelines for using them effectively, summarized from the book Classroom 
Assessment for Student Learning by Stiggins, Arter, Chapp uis and Chappuis. This 
summary was prepared by Liz Gewirtzman, a master “teacher of teachers” and 
member of the MEF team of consultants. When it is not obvious from the question 
itself, we let you know which category of assessment a particular question bel ongs to 
–  whether essay, fill in, or performance assessment. You can refer to these guidelines 
to find out more about each of the forms of assessment.  
5.   Our Team  
The Zekelman Standards for Chumash were developed by a team of educators under the 
auspices of the Menachem Education Foundation. The team is directed by Rabbi Yossi 
Rosenblum, principal of Yeshiva Schools, Pittsburgh, PA, and includes Rabbi Mendy 
Greenbaum, principal of Cheder Menachem, Los Angeles, CA ; Mrs. Sara Rosenfeld, 
curriculum director at Beth Rivka/Yeshiva Colleges of Melbourne, AU ; Rabbi Meir Perelstein, 
curriculum director at Darchei Menachem, Brooklyn, NY ; and Mrs. Chanah Rose, former 
curriculum director at the Shluchim Online School. All of these contributors, as well as the 
real time feedback from the schools they represent, helped to determine and refine the 
level of rigor intended by each standard. The assessment questions themselves were 
created by Rabbi Yossi Rosenblum and Mrs. Chanah Rose, incorporating questions by Rabbi 
Mendy Gr eenbaum and Mrs. Leah Hoffman as well.  
We would like to thank Mrs. Rena Udkoff for her expert editing of this document, and Rabbi 
Meir Perelstein for his layout and design. We would also like to thank the entire team at 
MEF, most notably Rabbi Zalman Shneu r, executive director, and Rabbi Shmuly  Goldman, 
vice president  and COO, for driving this process. Special appreciation is due to Mr. Alan 
Zekelman, a visionary philanthropist, for making the Zekelman Standards Project possible.  
We wish you, the teacher, m uch success in the implementation of these assessments and 
Hatzlacha in this most sacred task entrusted upon you, educating the next generation of 
Torah - true Jews.  
The Zekelman Standards Development Team

Now ’ ה appeared to him in אֵלֹנֵי מַמְרֵא and he was sitting at the entran ce of the tent when the day was hot. And he lifted his eyes 
and saw, and behold, three men were standing beside him, and he saw and he ran toward them from the entrance of the tent, and  
he bowed to the ground. And he said, "My masters, if I have found favo r in your eyes, please do not pass on from beside your 
servant.” Let now a little water be taken, and wash your feet, and rest yourselves under the tree. And I will take a morsel o f bread, 
and sustain your hearts; after, you should pass on, because you hav e passed by your servants." And they said, "So shall you do, as 
you have spoken"

א  הָאֹהֶל, כְּחֹם הַיּוֹם-יֹשֵׁב פֶּתַחוַיֵּרָא אֵלָיו ה', בְּאֵלֹנֵי מַמְרֵא; וְהוּא   . ב  וַיִּשָּׂא עֵינָיו, וַיַּרְא, וְהִנֵּה שְׁלֹשָׁה אֲנָשִׁים, נִצָּבִים עָלָיו; וַיַּרְא, וַיָּרָץ 
לִקְרָאתָם מִפֶּתַח הָאֹהֶל, וַיִּשְׁתַּחוּ, אָרְצָה   . ג  נָא תַעֲבֹר, מֵעַל עַבְדֶּךָ -אַל--בְּעֵינֶיךָ  נָא מָצָאתִי חֵן -אֲדֹנָי, אִם  וַיֹּאמַר:  ד  יֻקַּֽח־נָ֣א מְעַט־מַ֔יִם 
תַּ֥חַת הָעֵֽץ׃ וְרַֽחֲצ֖וּ רַגְלֵיכֶ֑ם וְהִֽשָּׁעֲנ֖וּ  
ה  כַּֽאֲשֶׁ֥ר דִּבַּֽרְתָּ׃ ן תַּֽעֲשֶׂ֖הוְאֶקְחָ֨ה פַת־לֶ֜חֶם וְסַֽעֲד֤וּ לִבְּכֶם֙ אַחַ֣ר תַּֽעֲבֹ֔רוּ כִּֽי־עַל־כֵּ֥ן עֲבַרְתֶּ֖ם עַֽל־עַבְדְּכֶ֑ם וַיֹּ֣אמְר֔וּ כֵּ֥  
 
Now ’ ה appeared to him in אֵלֹנֵי מַמְרֵא and he was sitting at the entrance of the tent when the day was hot. And he lifted his eyes 
and saw, and behold, three men were standing beside him, and he saw and he ran toward them fr om the entrance of the tent, and 
he bowed to the ground. And he said, "My masters, if I have found favor in your eyes, please do not pass on from beside your 
servant.” Let now a little water be taken, and wash your feet, and rest yourselves under the tree.  And I will take a morsel of bread, 
and sustain your hearts; after, you should pass on, because you have passed by your servants." And they said, "So shall you d o, as 
you have spoken"

א  הָאֹהֶל, כְּחֹם הַיּוֹם-וַיֵּרָא אֵלָיו ה', בְּאֵלֹנֵי מַמְרֵא; וְהוּא יֹשֵׁב פֶּתַח   . ב  וַיַּרְא, וַיָּרָץ וַיִּשָּׂא עֵינָיו, וַיַּרְא, וְהִנֵּה שְׁלֹשָׁה אֲנָשִׁים, נִצָּבִים עָלָיו; 
לִקְרָאתָם מִפֶּתַח הָאֹהֶל, וַיִּשְׁתַּחוּ, אָרְצָה   . ג  נָא תַעֲבֹר, מֵעַל עַבְדֶּךָ -אַל--בְּעֵינֶיךָ  נָא מָצָאתִי חֵן -אֲדֹנָי, אִם  וַיֹּאמַר:  ד  יֻקַּֽח־נָ֣א מְעַט־מַ֔יִם 
תַּ֥חַת הָעֵֽץ׃ וְרַֽחֲצ֖וּ רַגְלֵיכֶ֑ם וְהִֽשָּׁעֲנ֖וּ

Now ’ ה appeared to him in אֵלֹנֵי מַמְרֵא and he was sitting at the entrance of the tent when the day was hot. And he lifted his eyes 
and saw, and behold, three men were standing beside him, and he saw and he ran toward them from the entrance of the tent, and  
he bowed to the ground. And he said, "My masters, if I have found favor in your eyes,  please do not pass on from beside your 
servant.” Let now a little water be taken, and wash your feet, and rest yourselves under the tree. And I will take a morsel o f bread, 
and sustain your hearts; after, you should pass on, because you have passed by you r servants." And they said, "So shall you do, as 
you have spoken"

א וַיְהִי, אַחַר הַדְּבָרִים הָאֵלֶּה, וְהָאֱלֹהִים, נִסָּה אֶת-אַבְרָהָם; וַיֹּאמֶר אֵלָיו, אַבְרָהָם וַיֹּאמֶר הִנֵּנִי.  ב וַיֹּאמֶר קַח-נָא אֶת-בִּנְךָ אֶת-יְחִידְךָ 
אֲשֶׁר- אָהַבְתָּ, אֶת-יִצְחָק, וְלֶךְ -לְךָ, אֶל-אֶרֶץ הַמֹּרִיָּה; וְהַעֲלֵהוּ שָׁם, לְעֹלָה, עַל אַחַד הֶהָרִים, אֲשֶׁר אֹמַר אֵלֶיךָ.  ג וַיַּשְׁכֵּם אַבְרָהָם בַּבֹּקֶר, 
וַיַּחֲבֹשׁ אֶת-חֲמֹרוֹ, וַיִּקַּח אֶת-שְׁנֵי נְעָרָיו אִ תּוֹ, וְאֵת יִצְחָק בְּנוֹ; וַיְבַקַּע, עֲצֵי עֹלָה, וַיָּקָם וַיֵּלֶךְ, אֶל-הַמָּקוֹם אֲשֶׁר-אָמַר-לוֹ הָאֱלֹהִים.  ד בַּיּוֹם 
הַשְּׁלִישִׁי, וַיִּשָּׂא אַבְרָהָם אֶת-עֵינָיו וַיַּרְא אֶת-הַמָּקוֹם--מֵרָחֹק.  ה וַיֹּאמֶר אַבְרָהָם אֶל-נְעָרָיו, שְׁבוּ -לָכֶ ם פֹּה עִם-הַחֲמוֹר, וַאֲנִי וְהַנַּעַר, נֵלְכָה 
עַד-כֹּה; וְנִשְׁתַּחֲוֶה, וְנָשׁוּבָה אֲלֵיכֶם.  ו וַיִּקַּח אַבְרָהָם אֶת-עֲצֵי הָעֹלָה, וַיָּשֶׂם עַל-יִצְחָק בְּנוֹ, וַיִּקַּח בְּיָדוֹ, אֶת-הָאֵשׁ וְאֶת-הַמַּאֲכֶלֶת; וַיֵּלְכוּ 
שְׁנֵיהֶם, יַחְדָּו.  ז וַיֹּאמֶר יִצְחָק אֶל-אַבְרָהָם אָבִיו, וַיֹּאמֶר אָבִי, וַיֹּאמֶר, הִנֶּנִּי בְנִי; וַיֹּאמֶר, הִנֵּה הָאֵשׁ וְהָעֵצִים, וְאַיֵּה הַשֶּׂה, לְעֹלָה.  ח וַיֹּאמֶר, 
אַבְרָהָם, אֱלֹהִים יִרְאֶה-לּוֹ הַשֶּׂה לְעֹלָה, בְּנִי; וַיֵּלְכוּ שְׁנֵיהֶם, יַחְדָּו.   ט וַיָּבֹאוּ, אֶל-הַמָּקוֹם אֲשֶׁר אָמַר-לוֹ הָאֱלֹהִים, וַיִּבֶן שָׁם אַבְרָהָם אֶת- 
הַמִּזְבֵּחַ, וַיַּעֲרֹךְ אֶת-הָעֵצִים; וַיַּעֲקֹד, אֶת-יִצְחָק בְּנוֹ, וַיָּשֶׂם אֹתוֹ עַל-הַמִּזְבֵּחַ, מִמַּעַל לָעֵצִים.  י וַיִּשְׁלַח אַבְרָהָם אֶת-יָדוֹ, וַיִּקַּח אֶ ת-הַמַּאֲכֶלֶת, 
לִשְׁחֹט, אֶת-בְּנוֹ.  יא וַיִּקְרָא אֵלָיו מַלְאַךְ יְהוָה, מִן-הַשָּׁמַיִם, וַיֹּאמֶר, אַבְרָהָם אַבְרָהָם; וַיֹּאמֶר, הִנֵּנִי.  יב וַיֹּאמֶר, אַל-תִּשְׁלַח יָדְךָ אֶל-הַנַּעַר, 
וְאַל-תַּעַשׂ לוֹ, מְאוּמָה:  כִּי עַתָּה יָדַעְתִּי, כִּי-יְרֵא אֱלֹהִים אַתָּה, וְלֹא חָשַׂכְתָּ אֶת-בִּנְךָ אֶת-יְחִידְךָ, מִמֶּנִּי.   יג וַיִּשָּׂא אַבְרָהָם אֶת-עֵינָיו, וַיַּרְא 
וְהִנֵּה-אַיִל, אַחַר, נֶאֱחַז בַּסְּבַךְ בְּקַרְנָיו; וַיֵּלֶךְ אַבְרָהָם וַיִּקַּח אֶת-הָאַיִל, וַיַּעֲלֵהוּ לְעֹלָה תַּחַת בְּנוֹ.   יד וַיִּקְרָא אַבְרָהָם שֵׁם-הַמָּקוֹם הַהוּא, יְהוָה

4 .7  Noticing anomalies and deviations in the text  
Grade 1  Grade 2  Grade 3  Grade 4  Grade 5  Grade 6  Grade 7  Grade 8  
4.7   Noticing anomalies and deviations in the text  
 A. Recognizes 
seemingly 
extraneous 
language in 
the text after 
it was pointed 
out by the 
teacher, such 
as:  
  Repetition 
of words.  
  Repetition 
of syno - 
nyms.  
A. Recognizes extraneous 
language, such as:  
  Repetition of words.     
  Repetition of synonyms.  
And recognizes when facts are 
missing from the text.  
 
A. Recognizes other anomalies in the text and gaps in the text, 
including:  
  Missing subject.   
  Missing objects.  
  Incomplete sentences.  
  Missing and extra letters  
  Grammatical inconsistencies  
  Difficulties in the narrative and logical flow of the text

7.  In the following questions, we will compare the way Hashem described this journey with the way that אברהם described it.

b.  Who said -  that they ( אברהם ויצחק will serve ה on that mountain?  
i.  Only ה said.  
ii.  O nly אברהם said  
iii.  They both said this.  
c.  Who said -  that אברהם will offer יצחק as a קרבן  ? 
i.  Only ה said  
ii.  O nly אברהם said  
iii.  They both said this.  
d.  Who said -  that they ( אברהם ויצחק will return to the נערים after serving ה  ?' 
i.  Only ה said  
ii.  only אברהם said  
iii.  They both said this.

Performance Assessments:  
1.  Draw what was created on each of the 6 days of creation.  
2.  Together with your partners, act out what took place in י -ח, פסוק א ”בראשית, פרק י  . 
3.  Re - tell , as a דבר תורה the story of אדם and חוה eating from the עץ הדעת including what happened and lessons learned.  
4.  When יעקב left חרן to return to ל-ארץ ישרא what would he have taken along? Create a ‘showbag’ with items that would 
have been taken, and explain the importance of each item.  
5.  Create a diorama depicting the scene of יציאת מצרים Show as many details as you can that are found in the פסוקים  . 
6.  Create a  shield or flag, depicting the שבט s key character traits based on ברכות יעקב  . 
7.  What was it like to be a Jewish child watching the מכות take place? Write a series of three diary entries as though you were 
there, answering the question.
